  .iter()\n    75→                .position(|selector| {\n    76→                    // Does the entry belong to a different thread?\n    77→                    selector.cx.thread_id() != thread_id\n    78→                        && selector // Try selecting this operation.\n    79→                            .cx\n    80→                            .try_select(Selected::Operation(selector.oper))\n    81→                            .is_ok()\n    82→                        && {\n    83→                            // Provide the packet.\n    84→                            selector.cx.store_packet(selector.packet);\n    85→                            // Wake the thread up.\n    86→                            selector.cx.unpark();\n    87→                            true\n    88→                        }\n    89→                })\n    90→                // Remove the entry from the queue to keep it clean and improve\n    91→                // performance.\n    92→                .map(|pos| self.selectors.remove(pos))\n    93→        }\n    94→    }\n    95→\n    96→    /// Notifies all operations waiting to be ready.\n    97→    #[inline]\n    98→    pub(crate) fn notify(&mut self) {\n    99→        for entry in self.observers.drain(..) {\n   100→            if entry.cx.try_select(Selected::Operation(entry.oper)).is_ok() {\n   101→                entry.cx.unpark();\n   102→            }\n   103→        }\n   104→    }\n   105→\n   106→    /// Notifies all registered operations that the channel is disconnected.\n   107→    #[inline]\n   108→    pub(crate) fn disconnect(&mut self) {\n   109→        for entry in self.selectors.iter() {\n   110→            if entry.cx.try_select(Selected::Disconnected).is_ok() {\n   111→                // Wake the thread up.\n   112→                //\n   113→                // Here we don't remove the entry from the queue. simple wrapper around `Waker` that internally uses a mutex for synchronization.\n   135→pub(crate) struct SyncWaker {\n   136→    /// The inner `Waker`.\n   137→    inner: Mutex<Waker>,\n   138→\n   139→    /// `true` if the waker is empty.\n   140→    is_empty: Atomic<bool>,\n   141→}\n   142→\n   143→impl SyncWaker {\n   144→    /// Creates a new `SyncWaker`.\n   145→    #[inline]\n   146→    pub(crate) fn new() -> Self {\n   147→        SyncWaker { inner: Mutex::new(Waker::new()), is_empty: AtomicBool::new(true) }\n   148→    }\n   149→\n   150→    /// Registers the current thread with an inner.register(oper, cx);\n   155→        self.is_empty\n   156→            .store(inner.selectors.is_empty() && inner.observers.is_empty(), Ordering::SeqCst);\n   157→    }\n   158→\n   159→    /// Unregisters an operation previously registered by the current thread.\n   160→    #[inline]\n   161→    pub(crate) fn unregister(&self, oper: Operation) -> Option<Entry> {\n   162→        let mut inner = self.inner.lock().unwrap();\n   163→        let entry = inner.unregister(oper);\n   164→        self.is_empty\n   165→            .store(inner.selectors.is_empty() && inner.observers.is_empty(), Ordering::SeqCst);\n   166→        entry\n   167→    }\n   168→\n   169→    /// Attempts to find one thread (not the current one), select its operation, and wake it up.\n   170→    #[inline]\n   171→    pub(crate) fn notify(&self) {\n   172→        if !self.is_empty.load(Ordering::SeqCst) {\n   173→            let mut inner = self.inner.lock().unwrap();\n   174→ 185→    /// Notifies all threads that the channel is disconnected.\n   186→    #[inline]\n   187→    pub(crate) fn disconnect(&self) {\n   188→        let mut inner = self.inner.lock().unwrap();\n   189→        inner.disconnect();\n   190→        self.is_empty\n   191→            .store(inner.selectors.is_empty() && inner.observers.is_empty(), Ordering::SeqCst);\n   192→    }\n   193→}\n   194→\n Waking mechanism for threads blocked on channel operations.\n\nuse super::context::Context;\nuse super::select::{Operation, Selected};\nuse crate::ptr;\nuse crate::sync::Mutex;\nuse crate::sync::atomic::{Atomic, AtomicBool, Ordering};\n\n/// Represents a thread blocked on a specific channel operation.\npub(crate) struct Entry {\n    /// The operation.\n    pub(crate) oper: Operation,\n\n    /// Optional packet.\n    pub(crate) packet: *mut (),\n\n    /// Context associated with the thread owning this operation.\n    pub(crate) cx: Context,\n}\n\n/// A queue of threads blocked on channel operations.\n///\n/// This data structure is used by threads to register blocking operations and get woken up once\n/// an operation becomes ready.\npub(crate) struct Waker {\n    /// A list of select operations.\n    selectors: Vec<Entry>,\n\n    /// A list of operations waiting to be ready.\n    observers: Vec<Entry>,\n}\n\nimpl Waker {\n    /// Creates a new `Waker`.\n    #[inline]\n    pub(crate) fn new() -> Self {\n        Waker { selectors: Vec::new(), observers: Vec::new() }\n    }\n\n    /// Registers a select operation.\n    #[inline]\n    pub(crate) fn register(&mut self, oper: Operation, cx: &Context) {\n        self.register_with_packet(oper, ptr::null_mut(), cx);\n    }\n\n    /// Registers a select operation and a packet.\n    #[inline]\n    pub(crate) fn register_with_packet(&mut self, oper: Operation, packet: *mut (), cx: &Context) {\n        self.selectors.push(Entry { oper, packet, cx: cx.clone() });\n    }\n\n    /// Unregisters a select operation.\n    #[inline]\n    pub(crate) fn unregister(&mut self, oper: Operation) -> Option<Entry> {\n        if let Some((i, _)) =\n            self.selectors.iter().enumerate().find(|&(_, entry)| entry.oper == oper)\n        {\n            let entry = self.selectors.remove(i);\n            Some(entry)\n        } else {\n            None\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Attempts to find another thread's entry, select the operation, and wake it up.\n    #[inline]\n    pub(crate) fn try_select(&mut self) -> Option<Entry> {\n        if self.selectors.is_empty() {\n            None\n        } else {\n            let thread_id = current_thread_id();\n\n            self.selectors\n                .iter()\n                .position(|selector| {\n                    // Does the entry belong to a different thread?\n                    selector.cx.thread_id() != thread_id\n                        && selector // Try selecting this operation.\n                            .cx\n                            .try_select(Selected::Operation(selector.oper))\n                            .is_ok()\n                        && {\n                            // Provide the packet.\n                            selector.cx.store_packet(selector.packet);\n                            // Wake the thread up.\n                            selector.cx.unpark();\n                            true\n                        }\n                })\n                // Remove the entry from the queue to keep it clean and improve\n                // performance.\n                .map(|pos| self.selectors.remove(pos))\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Notifies all operations waiting to be ready.\n    #[inline]\n    pub(crate) fn notify(&mut self) {\n        for entry in self.observers.drain(..) {\n            if entry.cx.try_select(Selected::Operation(entry.oper)).is_ok() {\n                entry.cx.unpark();\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Notifies all registered operations that the channel is disconnected.\n    #[inline]\n    pub(crate) fn disconnect(&mut self) {\n        for entry in self.selectors.iter() {\n            if entry.cx.try_select(Selected::Disconnected).is_ok() {\n                // Wake the thread up.\n                //\n                // Here we don't remove the entry from the queue. Registered threads must\n                // unregister from the waker by themselves. They might also want to recover the\n                // packet value and destroy it, if necessary.\n                entry.cx.unpark();\n            }\n        }\n\n        self.notify();\n    }\n}\n\nimpl Drop for Waker {\n    #[inline]\n    fn drop(&mut self) {\n        debug_assert_eq!(self.selectors.len(), 0);\n        debug_assert_eq!(self.observers.len(), 0);\n    }\n}\n\n/// A waker that can be shared among threads without locking.\n///\n/// This is a simple wrapper around `Waker` that internally uses a mutex for synchronization.\npub(crate) struct SyncWaker {\n    /// The inner `Waker`.\n    inner: Mutex<Waker>,\n\n    /// `true` if the waker is empty.\n    is_empty: Atomic<bool>,\n}\n\nimpl SyncWaker {\n    /// Creates a new `SyncWaker`.\n    #[inline]\n    pub(crate) fn new() -> Self {\n        SyncWaker { inner: Mutex::new(Waker::new()), is_empty: AtomicBool::new(true) }\n    }\n\n    /// Registers the current thread with an operation.\n    #[inline]\n    pub(crate) fn register(&self, oper: Operation, cx: &Context) {\n        let mut inner = self.inner.lock().unwrap();\n        inner.register(oper, cx);\n        self.is_empty\n            .store(inner.selectors.is_empty() && inner.observers.is_empty(), Ordering::SeqCst);\n    }\n\n    /// Unregisters an operation previously registered by the current thread.\n    #[inline]\n    pub(crate) fn unregister(&self, oper: Operation) -> Option<Entry> {\n        let mut inner = self.inner.lock().unwrap();\n        let entry = inner.unregister(oper);\n        self.is_empty\n            .store(inner.selectors.is_empty() && inner.observers.is_empty(), Ordering::SeqCst);\n        entry\n    }\n\n    /// Attempts to find one thread (not the current one), select its operation, and wake it up.\n    #[inline]\n    pub(crate) fn notify(&self) {\n        if !self.is_empty.load(Ordering::SeqCst) {\n            let mut inner = self.inner.lock().unwrap();\n            if !self.is_empty.load(Ordering::SeqCst) {\n                inner.try_select();\n                inner.notify();\n                self.is_empty.store(\n                    inner.selectors.is_empty() && inner.observers.is_empty(),\n                    Ordering::SeqCst,\n                );\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Notifies all threads that the channel is disconnected.\n    #[inline]\n    pub(crate) fn disconnect(&self) {\n        let mut inner = self.inner.lock().unwrap();\n        inner.disconnect();\n        self.is_empty\n            .store(inner.selectors.is_empty() && inner.observers.is_empty(), Ordering::SeqCst);\n    }\n}\n\nimpl Drop for SyncWaker {\n    #[inline]\n    fn drop(&mut self) {\n        debug_assert!(self.is_empty.load(Ordering::SeqCst));\n    }\n}\n\n/// Returns a unique id for the current thread.\n#[inline]\npub fn current_thread_id() -> usize {\n    // `u8` is not drop so this variable will be available during thread destruction,\n    // whereas `thread::current()` would not be\n    thread_local! { static DUMMY: u8 = const { 0 } }\n    DUMMY.with(|x| (x as *const u8).addr())\n}\n","numLines":210,"startLine":1,"totalLines":210}}}

RawWaker contains a data pointer and a reference to a static RawWakerVTable, which is a virtual function pointer table defining clone, wake, wake_by_ref, and drop operations. This allows custom executor implementations to provide their own wakeup behavior without heap allocation.\\n\\n2. **Waker (library/core/src/task/wake.rs)**: A high-level wrapper around RawWaker that is Send and Sync. The Waker type encapsulates a RawWaker and provides safe methods like wake() and wake_by_ref() for waking up tasks. Both Waker and LocalWaker can be constructed from RawWaker instances using from_raw().\\n\\n4. **Context (library/core/src/task/wake.rs)**: The execution context passed to Future::poll(). This type is returned by Future::poll().\\n\\n7. **Future trait (library/core/src/future/future.rs)**: The core async abstraction with a poll() method that takes a Context and returns Poll<Output>. This is the fundamental interface that drives the polling loop in async runtimes.\\n\\n8. **poll_fn utility (library/core/src/future/poll_fn.rs)**: Provides PollFn struct and poll_fn() function for creating futures from custom polling functions, demonstrating how the polling mechanism works with custom logic.\\n\\nThe polling loop flow: An executor repeatedly calls Future::poll() with a Context containing a Waker. If a future returns Poll::Pending, it must store a clone of the Waker and call wake() on it when ready.
